35  
Results	  
In	  this	  section	  the	  results	  from	  the	  bioinformatics	  research	  as	  well	  as	  for	  the	  qPCR,	  IFN-­‐γ	  release	  
assay	  and	  Ipilimumab	  and	  Nivolumab	  binding	  assays	  will	  be	  presented.	  These	  assays	  aim	  to	  
investigate	  the	  cross	  reactivity	  of	  the	  human	  antibodies	  Ipilimumab	  and	  Nivolumab	  to	  porcine	  
lymphocytes	  as	  well	  as	  the	  ability	  to	  use	  the	  following	  in	  vitro	  methods	  to	  obtain	  the	  results.	  As	  
mentioned	  before	  human	  PBMCs	  were	  also	  used	  as	  a	  positive	  control	  in	  all	  methods.	  
Bioinformatics	  
Bioinformatic	  methods	  were	  used	  to	  find	  the	  protein	  version	  of	  CTLA-­‐4	  and	  PD-­‐1	  for	  both	  
human	  and	  pig	  sequences	  to	  align	  them	  and	  obtain	  the	  homology	  between	  them.	  	  
CTLA-­‐4	  
Figure	  13	  shows	  the	  result	  from	  the	  blast	  research	  and	  the	  identity	  of	  pig	  CTLA-­‐4	  is	  85,7%	  to	  
human	  CTLA-­‐4,	  which	  is	  higher	  compared	  to	  the	  identity	  of	  the	  mouse.	  	  
	  
	  
Figure	  13:	  part	  of	  the	  result	  from	  blasting	  the	  human	  CTLA-­‐4	  against	  all	  species	  obtained	  from	  
http://www.uniprot.org.	  
The	  alignment	  obtained	  from	  this	  research	  is	  shown	  in	  Figure	  14.	  
	  
	  
Figure	  14:	  The	  alignment	  between	  human	  and	  pig	  CTLA-­‐4	  obtained	  from	  
http://www.uniprot.org/blast/uniprot/B2015082264ZU3PLARX?fil=reviewed:yes.	  The	  UniProt	  identifying	  numbers	  
are	  shown	  at	  the	  left,	  homology	  is	  85,7%.	  
The	  extracellular	  domain	  of	  human	  CTLA-­‐4	  was	  also	  blasted	  against	  pig	  sequence.	  The	  
alignment	  is	  presented	  in	  Figure	  15.	  The	  identity	  of	  the	  extracellular	  domain	  is	  83.9%.	  
==PAGE:48==
	  
36  
	  
Figure	  15:	  Alignment	  of	  porcine	  extracellular	  domain	  to	  human	  extracellular	  domain	  obtained	  from	  
http://www.uniprot.org/blast/uniprot/B2015082274Z84Y9S5M?alignment=32	  at	  UniProt.org,	  the	  UniProt	  
identifying	  numbers	  are	  shown	  at	  the	  left,	  homology	  is	  83.9%.	  
The	  sequences	  was	  compared	  to	  investigate	  the	  sequences	  that	  are	  important	  for	  the	  binding	  of	  
CTLA-­‐4	  to	  B7	  and	  the	  sequence	  that	  is	  important	  for	  the	  binding	  of	  CTLA-­‐4	  to	  antibodies.	  The	  
alignment	  in	  Figure	  15	  shows	  that	  the	  sequence	  VNLT	  I	  Q	  G	  L	  is	  in	  fact	  conserved	  between	  
human	  and	  pig.	  However	  the	  sequence	  (MYPPPY)	  in	  human	  differs	  in	  one	  single	  amino	  acid	  (M)	  
versus	  (L).	  The	  binding	  sequence	  for	  pig	  is	  LYPPPY.	  	  
The	  different	  isoforms	  of	  CTLA-­‐4	  are	  shown	  in	  Figure	  16.	  They	  differ	  in	  the	  length	  of	  the	  
sequence	  as	  some	  of	  the	  isoforms	  are	  soluble	  or	  missing	  a	  specific	  peptide	  motif.	  	  
	  
	  
Figure	  16:	  the	  different	  isoforms	  of	  human	  CTLA-­‐4	  obtained	  from	  http://www.uniprot.org.	  except	  for	  the	  isoform	  1.	  
In	  this	  study	  isoform	  1	  was	  chosen	  due	  to	  it	  being	  the	  longest	  one	  and	  having	  the	  cytoplasmic,	  
transmembrane	  and	  extracellular	  domains.	  
PD-­‐1	  
Human	  PD-­‐1	  gene	  sequence	  was	  found	  in	  nucleotide	  NCBI	  in	  the	  same	  way	  as	  for	  CTLA-­‐4.	  The	  
complete	  CDS	  was	  found	  with	  the	  accession	  no.	  L27440	  and	  this	  gene	  was	  then	  blasted	  against	  
sus	  scrofa	  (pig)	  sequence.	  The	  search	  resulted	  in	  the	  NCBI	  Reference	  Sequence:	  
NM_001204379.1,	  (Sus	  scrofa	  programmed	  cell	  death	  1	  (PDCD1),	  mRNA).	  	  An	  alignment	  for	  the	  
protein	  sequence	  was	  made	  in	  EBI	  database	  where	  multiple	  sequence	  alignment	  was	  performed	  
by	  the	  program	  MAFFT.	  The	  alignment	  is	  shown	  in	  Figure	  17	  
==PAGE:49==
	  
37  
	  
Figure	  17:	  Alignment	  done	  by	  MAFFT	  program	  in	  CLUSTAL	  format.	  Stars	  denote	  identical	  amino	  acids	  in	  the	  two	  
sequences	  while	  “.”	  and	  “:”	  denote	  similarity,	  red	  color	  denote	  small	  hydrophobic	  amino	  acids,	  blue	  denotes	  Acidic,	  
magenta	  for	  basic,	  green	  for	  hydroxyl	  +	  sulfhydryl	  +	  amine	  +	  glycin	  and	  Grey	  denotes	  unusual	  amino	  acids.	  The	  
sequence	  with	  no:	  604541	  is	  the	  human	  version	  and	  the	  sequence	  no:	  324120925	  is	  the	  porcine	  version.	  The	  
homology	  between	  these	  protein	  sequences	  is	  63,99%.	  
The	  pig	  PD-­‐1	  protein	  sequence	  homology	  to	  human	  PD-­‐1	  is	  63,99%.	  Two	  sequences	  are	  
important	  in	  the	  matter	  of	  Nivolumab	  binding	  to	  human	  PD-­‐1.	  A	  study	  showed	  that	  there	  are	  
two	  peptides	  in	  human	  PD-­‐1,	  29SFVLNWYRMSPSNQTDKLAAFPEDR53	  and	  
85SGTYLCGAISLAPKAQIKE103,	  that	  bind	  to	  Nivolumab	  and	  that	  there	  are	  several	  residues	  that	  
are	  important	  in	  the	  PD-­‐1	  –	  PD-­‐L	  binding.	  These	  residues	  are	  part	  of	  the	  previous	  two	  
sequences(C.	  Wang	  et	  al.,	  2014).	  When	  comparing	  human	  and	  pig	  amino	  acid	  sequences	  in	  
Figure	  18,	  the	  alignment	  shows	  that	  although	  there	  is	  a	  high	  similarity	  between	  human	  and	  pig	  
sequences	  there	  are	  some	  amino	  acids	  that	  differ	  in	  the	  color	  but	  are	  still	  similar	  in	  their	  size	  
and	  function	  as	  they	  are	  denoted	  with	  (.	  ,	  :).	  
Figure	  18:	  comparison	  of	  the	  peptides	  important	  for	  the	  binding	  of	  Nivolumab	  to	  PD-­‐1	  in	  human	  (upper	  sequence)	  
and	  pig	  (lower	  sequence).	  Stars	  denote	  identical	  amino	  acids	  in	  the	  two	  sequences	  while	  “.”	  and	  “:”	  denote	  similarity,	  
red	  color	  denote	  small	  hydrophobic	  amino	  acids,	  blue	  denotes	  Acidic,	  magenta	  for	  basic,	  green	  for	  hydroxyl	  +	  
sulfhydryl	  +	  amine	  +	  glycin	  and	  Grey	  denotes	  unusual	  amino	  acids.	  
However	  sequence	  “A”	  pig	  sequence	  contains	  all	  hydrophobic	  amino	  acids	  that	  are	  in	  the	  human	  
version	  except	  one	  (p).	  In	  pig	  sequence	  B	  there	  is	  one	  hydrophobic	  amino	  acid	  (A)	  that	  differ.	  
The	  percent	  identity	  matrix	  created	  by	  Clustal	  2.1	  gives	  the	  sequence	  A	  in	  Figure	  18	  a	  similarity	  
of	  80%	  and	  a	  similarity	  of	  74%	  for	  sequence	  B.	  
qPCR	  
qPCR	  was	  performed	  to	  measure	  the	  expression	  of	  CTLA-­‐4	  and	  PD-­‐1	  genes	  upon	  stimulation	  in	  
porcine	  PBMC.	  Both	  human	  and	  porcine	  PBMCs	  were	  used	  to	  obtain	  mRNA,	  which	  was	  
reversibly	  transcribed	  into	  cDNA.	  To	  be	  able	  to	  conduct	  qPCR	  two	  sets	  of	  primers	  were	  designed	  
and	  tested	  to	  find	  the	  most	  efficient	  primer.	  The	  results	  in	  the	  following	  section	  contain	  the	  
results	  from	  the	  primer	  test,	  the	  efficiency	  test	  and	  the	  qPCR	  experiment.	  
A:	  
	  B:	  	  
	  
==PAGE:50==
	  
38  
Primer	  test	  
Two	  different	  primers	  for	  each	  gene	  in	  pig	  as	  well	  as	  human	  were	  tested	  to	  find	  the	  best	  primer	  
set	  with	  regard	  to	  product	  achievement,	  melting	  point	  (only	  one	  top)	  and	  efficacy	  	  
(approximately	  100%).	  This	  was	  done	  with	  samples	  collected	  after	  four	  and	  48	  hours	  incubation	  
with	  SEB	  to	  test	  DNA	  from	  both	  a	  short	  time	  incubation	  and	  longer	  time	  interval.	  All	  primers	  
showed	  productivity	  and	  one	  of	  the	  porcine	  primer	  set	  showed	  two	  amplification	  products	  with	  
two	  different	  melting	  points.	  Recording	  to	  these	  findings	  the	  following	  primer	  sets	  were	  chosen:	  
Primer	  name	   	  
	  
Primer	  sequence	  	  
Human-­‐CTLA-­‐4-­‐forw1	  	  
5’-­‐TCTGCAAAGCAATGCACGTG-­‐3’	  
	  
Human-­‐CTLA-­‐4-­‐rev1	   	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  	  5’-­‐TTGCCTGGAGATGCATACTC-­‐3’	  
	  
	  
	  
Porcine-­‐CTLA-­‐4-­‐forw2	  	  
5’-­‐CAAGTTGGAGCTCCTGTAC-­‐3’	  
	  
Porcine-­‐CTLA-­‐4-­‐rev2	   	  
5’-­‐ATGGTTCTGGATCAATGACATA-­‐3’	   	  
	  
	  
Human-­‐PD-­‐1-­‐forw1	  
	  
5’-­‐CAGCGGCACCTACCTCTG-­‐3’	  	  
	  
Human-­‐PD-­‐1-­‐rev1	  
	  
5’-­‐CTGCCCTTCTCTCTGTCAC-­‐3’	  
	  
	  
	  
Porcine-­‐PD-­‐1-­‐forw1	  
	  
5’-­‐ACAGTGGCACCTACTTCTGT-­‐3’	  
	  
Porcine-­‐PD-­‐1-­‐rev1	  
	  
5’-­‐CCAGGACTCTCTCTGTCAC-­‐3’	  
	  
	  
Efficiency	  analysis	  
R2	  and	  efficiency	  of	  the	  primers	  were	  determined	  for	  samples	  from	  48	  hours	  and	  94	  hours	  
incubation	  for	  the	  human	  CTLA-­‐4,	  PD-­‐1.	  For	  the	  test	  of	  Pig	  CTLA-­‐4,	  and	  PD-­‐1,	  samples	  from	  48	  
hours	  and	  72	  hours	  incubation	  were	  used.	  10-­‐fold	  serial	  dilution	  in	  six	  points	  in	  duplicates	  was	  
performed	  and	  NTCs	  were	  used	  as	  a	  negative	  control	  and	  to	  determine	  the	  CT	  threshold.	  The	  
difference	  between	  the	  qPCR	  for	  the	  different	  samples	  is	  that	  samples	  from	  48	  hours	  incubation	  
are	  not	  run	  in	  duplicates.	  
Amplification	  curves	  and	  standard	  curves	  as	  well	  as	  melting	  point	  curves	  were	  obtained.	  	  R2	  was	  
found	  from	  the	  linear	  regression	  function	  and	  E	  was	  calculated	  by	  the	  rotor-­‐gene	  Q	  program.	  	  
Porcine	  CTLA-­‐4	  primer	  set	  
For	  the	  porcine	  CTLA-­‐4	  primer	  set,	  samples	  from	  72	  hours	  were	  used	  and	  these	  have	  a	  better	  
efficiency	  as	  more	  than	  two	  points	  were	  obtained	  with	  an	  exponential	  doubling	  in	  DNA	  products.	  
In	  these	  samples	  R2	  was	  0.98	  and	  E	  was	  1.4	  (compared	  to	  E	  =	  1	  being	  100%	  efficiency).	  Figures	  
19	  and	  20	  show	  the	  standard	  and	  amplification	  plots	  for	  the10	  fold	  serial	  dilution	  of	  these	  
samples.	  	  
	  
Figure	  19:	  standard	  curve	  for	  porcine	  CTLA-­‐4	  for	  ten	  fold	  serial	  dilution.	  
	  
==PAGE:51==
	  
39

Porcine	  PD-­‐1	  primer	  set	  
The	  porcine	  PD-­‐1	  primer	  set	  was	  tested	  in	  to	  different	  samples	  as	  mentioned	  before.	  The	  best	  
results	  are	  obtained	  from	  48	  hours	  incubation	  samples.	  In	  these	  samples	  R2	  was	  0,99	  and	  E	  was	  
1.4.	  Figures	  21	  and	  22	  show	  the	  standard	  and	  amplification	  plots	  for	  the	  ten	  fold	  serial	  dilution	  
of	  these	  samples.

Figure	  22:	  standard	  curve	  for	  porcine	  PD-­‐1	  for	  ten	  fold	  serial	  dilution	  of	  48	  hours	  incubated	  samples.	  
Human	  CTLA-­‐4	  primer	  set	  
The	  efficiency	  test	  for	  the	  human	  primers	  showed	  a	  good	  efficiency	  in	  both	  94	  hours	  (E=	  1.2)	  
and	  48	  hours	  (E=1.1)	  samples.	  Figures	  23	  and	  24	  introduce	  the	  amplification	  plot	  and	  standard	  
curve	  for	  48	  hours	  as	  it	  shows	  the	  highest	  efficiency.	  In	  these	  samples	  R2	  was	  1	  and	  E	  was	  1.1.	  	  
	  
Figure	  23:	  amplification	  plot	  for	  human	  CTLA-­‐4	  for	  ten	  fold	  serial	  dilution	  of	  48	  hours	  incubated	  samples	  
	  
Figure	  24:	  Standard	  curve	  for	  human	  CTLA-­‐4	  for	  ten	  fold	  serial	  dilution	  of	  48	  hours	  incubated	  samples

Human	  PD-­‐1	  primer	  set	  
The	  efficiency	  test	  for	  the	  human	  primers	  showed	  a	  good	  efficiency	  in	  both	  94	  hours	  and	  48	  
hours	  samples,	  E=	  0.93	  and	  E=	  1.1	  respectively.	  In	  Figures	  25	  and	  26	  the	  amplification	  plot	  and	  
standard	  curve	  for	  94	  hours	  are	  presented,	  as	  it	  shows	  the	  highest	  efficiency.	  In	  these	  samples	  R2	  
was	  0.97	  and	  E	  was	  0.93.

Reference	  gene	  analysis	  
To	  test	  the	  efficiency	  of	  the	  reference	  genes,	  the	  expressions	  of	  Glyceraldehyde-­‐3-­‐phosphate	  
dehydrogenase	  (GAPDH)	  and	  ß-­‐actin	  were	  measured	  for	  both	  human	  and	  porcine	  samples	  by	  
qPCR.	  Both	  un-­‐stimulated	  and	  48	  hours	  stimulated	  samples	  were	  used,	  the	  samples	  were	  diluted	  
ten	  times	  and	  100	  times	  and	  a	  qPCR	  was	  performed.	  This	  primary	  test	  showed	  that	  GAPDH	  
having	  two	  peaks,	  meaning	  two	  products	  with	  two	  melting	  points.	  As	  for	  ß-­‐actin,	  it	  showed	  
productivity	  and	  only	  one	  melting	  point.	  An	  efficiency	  test	  for	  ß-­‐actin	  primer	  set	  was	  done	  with	  
the	  humane	  samples	  as	  it	  was	  designed	  from	  porcine	  gene.	  A	  10-­‐fold	  serial	  dilution	  in	  six	  points	  
from	  94	  hours	  stimulation	  was	  used.	  The	  results	  of	  the	  efficiency	  test	  are	  shown	  in	  Figures	  27	  
and	  28.	  All	  6	  points	  are	  shown	  in	  the	  graphs,	  and	  the	  R2=0.98	  and	  E=	  0.92.	  
	  
	  
Figure	  27:	  amplification	  plot	  for	  human	  ß-­‐actin	  for	  ten	  fold	  serial	  dilution	  of	  94	  hours	  incubated	  samples	  
	  
Figure	  28:	  Standard	  curve	  for	  human	  ß-­‐actin	  for	  ten	  fold	  serial	  dilution	  of	  94	  hours	  incubated	  samples	  
Real-­‐Time	  polymerase	  chain	  reaction	  (qPCR)	  assay	  
To	  study	  the	  gene	  expression	  of	  CTLA-­‐4	  and	  PD-­‐1	  genes	  in	  porcine	  and	  compare	  it	  to	  the	  gene	  
expression	  in	  human,	  qPCR	  was	  used.	  	  
==PAGE:53==
	  
41  
The	  samples	  used	  were	  taken	  from	  seven	  different	  time	  intervals	  (0,	  2,	  4,	  24,	  48,	  72	  and	  94	  
hours).	  These	  samples	  were	  made	  in	  triplicates.	  After	  setting	  the	  threshold	  according	  to	  the	  NTC,	  
the	  chosen	  threshold	  for	  all	  samples	  was	  0.05.	  All	  samples	  had	  one	  melting	  point,	  which	  indicate	  
both	  purity	  of	  samples	  and	  the	  efficiency	  of	  the	  primers.	  Figure	  29	  shows	  the	  amplification	  plots	  
for	  human	  CTLA-­‐4,	  PD-­‐1	  and	  ß-­‐actin	  and	  Figure	  30	  shows	  the	  amplification	  plots	  for	  porcine	  
CTLA-­‐4,	  PD-­‐1	  and	  ß-­‐actin.	  
	  
	  
	  
	  
Figure	  29:	  amplification	  plots	  for	  the	  human	  PD-­‐1	  gen	  products	  (A)	  and	  the	  CTLA-­‐4	  gen	  product	  (B)	  and	  ß-­‐actin	  (C)	  
obtained	  from	  the	  qPCR.	  
Figure	  30:	  	  amplification	  plots	  for	  the	  porcine	  PD-­‐1	  gen	  products	  (A)	  and	  the	  CTLA-­‐4	  gen	  product	  (B)	  and	  ß-­‐actin	  (C)	  
obtained	  from	  the	  qPCR.	  
Data	  was	  collected	  and	  exported	  to	  excel	  where	  data	  analysis	  was	  performed.	  The	  mean	  for	  all	  
three	  duplicates	  was	  calculated	  as	  well	  as	  the	  standard	  deviation	  (SD).	  The	  values	  from	  the	  
duplicates	  were	  very	  similar	  with	  low	  standard	  deviation	  except	  for	  one	  sample	  where	  the	  
deviated	  value	  was	  excluded	  and	  mean	  was	  calculated	  from	  the	  two	  other	  values.	  That	  is	  why	  
the	  mean	  value	  was	  used	  to	  normalize	  the	  expression	  of	  the	  genes.	  The	  obtained	  CT	  values	  from	  
the	  qPCR	  were	  compared	  to	  the	  standard	  curves	  from	  the	  efficiency	  test.	  The	  CT	  values	  that	  were	  
obtained	  from	  the	  qPCR,	  with	  all	  the	  samples	  were	  within	  the	  standard	  curve	  CT	  interval.	  For	  
example	  porcine	  CTLA-­‐4	  obtained	  CT	  values	  were	  between	  27	  and	  30,	  the	  standard	  curve	  for	  
porcine	  CTLA-­‐4	  was	  found	  from	  points	  with	  CT	  values	  between	  24	  and	  30	  cycles.	  This	  adds	  to	  the	  
reliability	  of	  the	  qPCR	  results.	  The	  Pfaffl	  method	  was	  used	  to	  normalize	  the	  results	  and	  analyze

the	  data	  as	  described	  in	  data	  analysis	  section.	  Figure	  31	  shows	  the	  results	  from	  the	  data	  analysis	  
of	  porcine	  samples.	  The	  result	  for	  the	  pig	  expression	  of	  PD-­‐1	  gens	  indicates	  that	  there	  was	  an	  
increase	  in	  expression	  upon	  stimulation	  already	  after	  two	  hours.	  After	  48	  hours	  of	  stimulation	  
the	  expression	  reached	  eight	  times	  higher	  then	  the	  start	  level.	  The	  expression	  level	  began	  to	  
decrease	  after	  three	  days	  but	  still	  not	  to	  the	  base	  level	  of	  expression	  at	  time	  point	  zero	  with	  no	  
SEB.	  Pig	  CTLA-­‐4	  expression	  was	  slightly	  and	  slowly	  elevated	  with	  time	  until	  48	  hours	  after	  
stimulation.	  After	  48	  hours	  incubation	  with	  SEB	  CTLA-­‐4	  expression	  seemed	  to	  increase	  rapidly	  
to	  reach	  12	  fold	  increase	  after	  four	  days.	  
	  
	  
Figure	  31:	  the	  change	  in	  expression	  of	  both	  CTLA-­‐4	  and	  PD-­‐1	  gens	  over	  time	  with	  and	  without	  SEB	  as	  a	  stimulant.	  	  
	  
	  
Figure	  32:	  The	  change	  in	  expression	  of	  both	  CTLA-­‐4	  and	  PD-­‐1	  gens	  over	  time	  with	  and	  without	  SEB	  as	  a	  stimulant.	  	  
The	  human	  expression	  of	  CTLA-­‐4	  and	  PD-­‐1	  over	  time	  is	  shown	  in	  Figure	  32.	  The	  results	  indicate	  
that	  SEB	  stimulated	  the	  expression	  of	  PD-­‐1	  in	  human	  cells	  and	  induced	  an	  increase	  in	  the	  
expression	  already	  after	  two	  hours	  to	  reach	  10-­‐fold	  increase.	  This	  increase	  is	  higher	  than	  the	  
one	  seen	  in	  pig	  and	  was	  also	  obtained	  faster.	  The	  increase	  intends	  to	  continue	  and	  reach	  the	  
maximum	  after	  24	  hours.	  The	  expression	  kept	  a	  high	  level	  through	  the	  incubation	  period	  of	  four	  
days.	  	  
Human	  CTLA-­‐4	  had	  a	  similar	  pattern	  to	  the	  porcine	  CTLA-­‐4.	  CTLA-­‐4	  expression	  was	  slightly	  and	  
slowly	  elevated	  with	  time	  until	  72	  hours	  after	  stimulation.	  After	  that	  the	  expression	  seemed	  to	  
double	  from	  day	  three	  to	  day	  four.	  
==PAGE:55==
	  
43  
Although	  the	  pattern	  seemed	  to	  be	  similar	  in	  pig	  and	  human	  the	  change	  fold	  is	  different.	  In	  
human	  PD-­‐1	  expression	  increased	  up	  to	  approximately	  16	  times	  as	  for	  the	  pig	  it	  reached	  
maximum	  fold	  change	  of	  8.	  For	  CTLA-­‐4	  expression	  in	  human	  the	  maximum	  was	  reached	  after	  
four	  days	  where	  there	  was	  observed	  around	  8-­‐fold	  change.	  Porcine	  CTLA-­‐4	  reached	  the	  highest	  
change	  fold	  of	  around	  12	  after	  four	  days.	  	  
IFN-­‐γ	  release	  assay	  
	  
Multiple	  IFN-­‐γ	  release	  assays	  were	  conducted	  in	  this	  study	  to	  measure	  the	  production	  of	  IFN-­‐γ	  
upon	  stimulation	  and	  blocking	  with	  the	  human	  checkpoint	  inhibitor	  antibodies	  Ipilimumab	  and	  
Nivolumab.	  Cells	  from	  the	  same	  pig	  and	  the	  same	  blood	  donor	  were	  used	  in	  all	  assays.	  After	  
stimulation	  with	  SEB,	  blocking	  with	  Ipilimumab	  and	  Nivolumab	  and	  incubation	  at	  different	  time	  
intervals,	  ELISA	  method	  was	  conducted	  and	  optimized	  systematically	  to	  obtain	  biologically	  
readable	  results.	  The	  primary	  ELISA	  optimization	  was	  done	  with	  porcine	  PBMCs,	  see	  workflow	  
in	  Appendix	  7.	  The	  porcine	  ELISA	  protocol	  was	  tested	  before	  by	  the	  staff	  at	  the	  veterinary	  
institute	  at	  DTU	  and	  believed	  to	  be	  efficient.	  	  
Porcine	  IFN-­‐γ	  release	  assay	  optimization	  
The	  first	  ELISA	  experiment	  was	  performed	  with	  PBMCs	  stimulated	  with	  three	  different	  
concentrations	  SEB	  or	  without	  SEB	  as	  shown	  in	  Table	  8.	  These	  PBMCs	  were	  also	  treated	  either	  
with	  Ipilimumab,	  Nivolumab	  (with	  four	  different	  concentrations)	  or	  with	  no	  checkpoint	  
blockade.

This	  first	  assay	  resulted	  in	  low	  concentrations	  of	  IFN-­‐γ	  as	  well	  as	  concentrations	  that	  were	  
independent	  of	  the	  SEB	  stimulations	  or	  checkpoint	  inhibition	  blockade.	  Thus	  the	  result	  indicated	  
the	  need	  of	  longer	  incubation	  time	  as	  well	  as	  higher	  concentrations	  of	  Ipilimumab	  and	  
Nivolumab.	  This	  led	  to	  the	  second	  experiment.	  Table	  9	  shows	  the	  experiment	  setup	  for	  the	  next	  
experiment.	  Here	  the	  cells	  were	  stimulated	  at	  time	  zero	  and	  at	  time	  24	  with	  the	  different	  SEB	  
concentrations.	  This	  experiment	  showed	  concentrations	  that	  were	  above	  the	  highest	  
concentration	  in	  the	  standard	  curve	  which	  made	  the	  results	  difficult	  to	  read	  and	  unreliable.	  The	  
concentrations	  showed	  neither	  systematic	  pattern	  upon	  stimulation	  nor	  blockade.	  These	  results	  
led	  us	  to	  the	  final	  experiment	  that	  was	  conducted	  with	  diluted	  samples.

Table	  10	  shows	  the	  final	  setup	  for	  the	  porcine	  IFN-­‐γ	  release	  assay.	  In	  this	  IFN-­‐γ	  release	  assay	  
only	  two	  concentrations	  SEB	  were	  chosen	  to	  be	  stimulated	  with,	  three	  different	  concentrations	  
Ipilimumab	  and	  Nivolumab,	  where	  stimulation	  and	  blockade	  were	  performed	  once	  at	  time	  zero.	  
The	  assay	  was	  also	  done	  with	  a	  combination	  of	  Ipilimumab	  and	  Nivolumab	  to	  study	  the	  in	  vitro	  
immune	  effect	  of	  the	  combination	  of	  these	  antibodies.	  
In	  the	  final	  assay	  with	  porcine	  PBMCs,	  samples	  from	  day	  one	  were	  not	  diluted;	  samples	  from	  day	  
two	  and	  three	  were	  20	  x	  diluted.	  This	  dilution	  factor	  was	  used	  to	  obtain	  concentrations	  that	  are	  
within	  the	  standard	  curve	  interval.	  Experiment	  two	  was	  used	  to	  suggest	  the	  dilution	  factor	  for	  
the	  final	  experiment.

Results	  from	  porcine	  IFN-­‐γ	  release	  assay	  final	  experiment.	  
Six	  plates	  were	  used	  in	  the	  ELISA	  assay	  to	  measure	  the	  OD	  and	  afterwards	  the	  concentrations	  
based	  on	  an	  IFN-­‐γ	  standard	  curve.	  In	  each	  plate	  the	  standard	  pooled	  pig	  IFN-­‐γ	  was	  also	  added	  in	  
a	  starting	  concentration	  of	  569	  pg/ml	  and	  in	  two	  fold	  serial	  dilution	  all	  the	  way	  down	  to	  35	  
pg/ml.	  The	  standard	  curve	  was	  calculated	  by	  plotting	  the	  logarithm	  of	  the	  measured	  OD-­‐values	  
from	  the	  ELISA	  read	  as	  a	  function	  of	  the	  logarithm	  to	  the	  standard	  concentrations.	  By	  doing	  that,	  
the	  formula	  y=ax+b	  was	  obtained,	  where	  y	  is	  the	  logarithm	  to	  the	  measured	  OD	  and	  x	  is	  the	  
logarithm	  to	  the	  IFN-­‐γ	  concentration.	  See	  Figure	  33	  for	  the	  standard	  curve	  of	  one	  of	  the	  plates.	  
This	  function	  is	  then	  used	  to	  calculate	  the	  logarithm	  of	  the	  concentrations	  of	  IFN-­‐γ	  that	  are	  
produced	  by	  the	  porcine	  PBMCs	  in	  all	  samples.	  Out	  of	  the	  obtained	  logarithms,	  the	  actual	  
concentrations	  were	  calculated	  and	  then	  multiplied	  with	  the	  dilution	  factors	  to	  get	  the	  real	  
concentrations.	  Due	  to	  the	  fact	  that	  duplicates	  were	  made	  of	  each	  sample	  the	  average	  of	  the	  
concentration	  was	  then	  calculated	  and	  the	  standard	  deviation	  was	  found.	  The	  concentrations	  
calculated	  before	  multiplying	  with	  the	  dilution	  factor	  were	  within	  the	  concentration	  interval	  of	  
the	  standard	  curve,	  which	  gives	  us	  readable	  and	  reliable	  results.	  
	  
Figure	  33:	  standard	  curve	  from	  plate	  1B,	  this	  standard	  curve	  is	  represenTable	  for	  concentrations	  in	  the	  interval	  
562,7-­‐35,1	  pg/ml.	  	  
The	  results	  of	  this	  assay	  is	  presented	  by	  using	  the	  data	  from	  day	  three	  with	  the	  SEB	  
concentration	  of	  0.1	  µg/ml	  and	  Ipilimumab	  and	  Nivolumab	  concentration	  of	  20	  µg/ml	  as	  these	  
==PAGE:57==
	  
45  
results	  show	  the	  highest	  immune	  response	  of	  PBMCs	  upon	  stimulation	  and	  blockade	  of	  
checkpoints.	  Figure	  34	  represents	  the	  charts	  with	  both	  porcine	  and	  human	  results;	  in	  this	  
section	  only	  porcine	  results	  are	  described.	  
	  
Figure	  34:	  Results	  from	  IFN-­‐ɣ	  release	  in	  both	  human	  and	  porcine	  PBMCs	  after	  three	  days	  incubation	  with	  0.1	  µg/ml	  
SEB	  and	  with	  or	  with	  out	  checkpoint	  blocking	  antibodies.	  Ipi	  stands	  for	  (Ipilimumab),	  Nivo	  stands	  for	  (Nivolumab).	  	  
The	  result	  shows	  a	  production	  of	  IFN-­‐γ	  upon	  stimulation	  with	  SEB,	  independent	  of	  the	  addition	  
of	  the	  checkpoint	  inhibitor	  blockers	  Ipilimumab	  or	  Nivolumab.	  The	  cells	  produce	  around	  4000	  
pg/ml	  IFN-­‐γ	  after	  three	  days	  stimulation.	  There	  is	  an	  increase	  in	  this	  production	  upon	  the	  
incubation	  with	  Ipilimumab,	  Nivolumab	  and	  Ipilimumab	  +	  Nivolumab,	  with	  concentrations	  of	  
approximately	  12000	  pg/ml,	  17000	  pg/ml	  and	  11000	  pg/ml	  respectively.	  The	  results	  indicate	  
that	  Nivolumab	  has	  the	  highest	  impact	  on	  porcine	  lymphocytes	  and	  stimulates	  them	  to	  produce	  
around	  four	  times	  more	  IFN-­‐	  γ.	  
The	  data	  of	  this	  assay	  was	  also	  analyzed	  for	  the	  samples	  with	  no	  stimulation,	  as	  shown	  in	  Figure	  
35.	  
	  
	  
Figure	  35:	  chart	  over	  results	  from	  IFN-­‐γ	  release	  assay	  data	  collected	  from	  un-­‐stimulated	  samples	  incubated	  with	  or	  
without	  different	  concentrations	  of	  Ipilimumab,	  Nivolumab	  and	  Ipilimumab	  +	  Nivolumab.	  The	  presented	  data	  is	  
collected	  from	  three	  days	  incubation	  (day	  one	  left	  –	  day	  three	  right).	  
==PAGE:58==
	  
46  
The	  results	  indicate	  that	  after	  24	  hours	  incubation	  with	  the	  blocking	  antibodies	  and	  with	  no	  
stimulation	  there	  is	  a	  low	  basic	  IFN-­‐γ	  production.	  After	  two	  days	  incubation	  an	  increase	  in	  the	  
production	  of	  IFN-­‐γ	  was	  observed	  in	  all	  samples	  including	  the	  untreated	  PBMCs	  however,	  
samples	  that	  are	  treated	  with	  Ipilimumab	  or	  Nivolumab	  or	  both	  show	  a	  higher	  increase	  of	  IFN-­‐γ	  
production.	  IFN-­‐γ	  production	  in	  day	  three	  varies	  for	  the	  different	  samples	  and	  shows	  high	  
increase	  in	  IFN-­‐γ	  production	  in	  the	  untreated	  samples	  as	  well	  as	  the	  other	  samples.	  	  
In	  another	  IFN-­‐γ	  release	  assay	  performed	  prior	  to	  this	  study	  by	  Zina	  Adil	  Al-­‐Shatrawi,	  an	  isotype	  
antibody	  (human	  IgG1	  κ	  isotype	  control	  antibody,	  GeneTex)	  that	  is	  similar	  to	  Ipilimumab	  
isotype	  was	  used	  in	  a	  concentration	  of	  2	  µg/ml	  as	  a	  control.	  This	  isotope	  was	  used	  to	  ensure	  that	  
the	  reaction	  that	  occurs	  is	  due	  to	  the	  binding	  of	  Ipilimumab	  to	  lymphocytes	  and	  not	  due	  to	  a	  
random	  overreaction	  towards	  Ipilimumab.	  The	  result	  of	  this	  assay	  indicated	  that	  the	  isotype	  do	  
not	  induce	  production	  of	  IFN-­‐γ	  and	  that	  IFN-­‐γ	  concentration	  obtained	  from	  the	  samples	  with	  the	  
isotype	  is	  almost	  similar	  to	  the	  samples	  with	  PBS	  see	  Figure	  36.	  	  
	  
Figure	  36:results	  from	  earlier	  study	  that	  investigated	  the	  effect	  of	  Ipilimumab	  on	  stimulated	  cells,	  this	  study	  also	  
shows	  that	  if	  incubated	  with	  an	  isotype	  that	  is	  similar	  to	  Ipilimumab	  the	  production	  level	  of	  IFN-­‐γis	  the	  same	  as	  for	  
the	  PBS	  (negative	  control)	  sample.	  
Human	  ELISA	  optimization	  
The	  IFN-­‐γ	  release	  assay	  that	  was	  performed	  with	  the	  human	  PBMCs	  uses	  the	  exact	  same	  method	  
as	  in	  the	  final	  assay	  for	  the	  porcine	  PBMCs.	  PBMCs	  from	  one	  blood	  donor	  were	  used.	  
The	  optimization	  process	  that	  was	  carried	  out	  on	  the	  ELISA	  involved	  different	  capture	  IFN-­‐γ	  
monoclonal	  antibodies,	  different	  blocking	  and	  dilution	  regents	  and	  different	  biotin	  conjugated	  
secondary	  IFN-­‐γ	  antibodies	  to	  obtain	  readable	  results.	  The	  results	  of	  the	  optimization	  processes	  
are	  presented	  in	  Table	  11.

Results	  from	  human	  IFN-­‐γ	  release	  assay	  final	  experiment.	  
The	  final	  ELISA	  was	  carried	  out	  with	  a	  duoSet	  ELISA	  development	  system	  and	  this	  gave	  the	  
following	  results.	  
In	  the	  human	  ELISA	  six	  plates	  were	  used	  measure	  the	  OD	  and	  afterwards	  the	  concentrations	  
based	  on	  an	  IFN-­‐γ	  standard	  curve.	  In	  each	  plate	  the	  standard	  human	  IFN-­‐γ	  Standard	  (from	  a	  
duoSet	  ELISA	  development	  system,	  R&D	  SYSTEMS).	  The	  standard	  was	  made	  with	  seven-­‐point	  
standard	  curve	  using	  2-­‐fold	  serial	  dilutions	  with	  the	  starting	  concentration	  of	  1000	  pg/ml	  and	  
end	  concentration	  of	  16	  pg/ml.	  The	  last	  two	  wells	  were	  filled	  with	  PBS	  to	  be	  used	  as	  a	  negative	  
control.	  	  All	  samples	  and	  standards	  were	  made	  as	  duplicates.	  The	  OD	  density	  was	  determined	  
and	  the	  data	  analysis	  was	  done	  in	  the	  exact	  same	  way	  as	  for	  the	  porcine	  samples.	  Figure	  37	  
presents	  the	  standard	  curve	  in	  one	  of	  the	  plates	  with	  the	  ODs	  of	  the	  human	  IFN-­‐gamma.	  The	  
concentrations	  calculated	  before	  multiplying	  with	  the	  dilution	  factor	  were	  with	  in	  the	  
concentration	  interval	  of	  the	  standard	  curve	  (16	  pg/ml	  –	  1000	  pg/ml),	  which	  gives	  readable	  and	  
reliable	  results.	  
	  
Figure	  37:	  standard	  curve	  from	  plate	  1A	  for	  human	  samples,	  this	  standard	  curve	  is	  represenTable	  for	  concentrations	  
in	  the	  interval	  503,4-­‐16,4	  pg/ml.	  
Similar	  to	  the	  porcine	  assay,	  the	  human	  IFN-­‐γ	  concentration	  obtained	  from	  the	  stimulation	  and	  
blockade	  assay	  were	  presented	  in	  this	  study	  for	  day	  three	  with	  the	  SEB	  concentration	  of	  0.1	  
µg/ml	  and	  Ipilimumab	  and	  Nivolumab	  concentration	  of	  20µg/ml.	  Figure	  34	  represents	  the	  
charts	  with	  both	  porcine	  and	  human	  results;	  in	  this	  section	  only	  human	  results	  are	  described.	  
IFN-­‐γ	  production	  in	  human	  samples	  stimulated	  with	  0.1µg/ml	  SEB	  and	  no	  blocking	  antibodies	  
showed	  a	  concentration	  of	  IFN-­‐γ	  of	  approximately	  11,000	  pg/ml.	  When	  incubating	  with	  blocking	  
antibodies	  the	  results	  indicate	  a	  higher	  production	  of	  IFN-­‐	  γ.	  When	  stimulating	  with	  SEB	  and	  
blocking	  with	  Ipilimumab	  for	  three	  days	  the	  IFN-­‐γ	  concentration	  in	  these	  samples	  reach	  
approximately	  18,000	  pg/ml.	  When	  blocking	  with	  Nivolumab	  the	  concentration	  reaches	  around	  
16,500	  pg/ml	  and	  when	  blocking	  with	  both	  antibodies	  the	  concentration	  of	  IFN-­‐γ	  increases	  up	  
to	  approximately	  22,000	  pg/ml.	  One	  needs	  to	  take	  into	  account	  the	  standard	  deviation	  as	  well	  as	  
==PAGE:60==
	  
48  
other	  factors	  that	  will	  be	  discussed	  later.	  As	  for	  the	  samples	  with	  no	  stimulation	  with	  SEB	  that	  
contains	  checkpoint	  inhibitor	  blockers,	  Figure	  38	  presents	  the	  results.

Figure	  38:	  chart	  over	  results	  from	  IFN-­‐γrelease	  assay	  data	  collected	  from	  un-­‐stimulated	  samples	  incubated	  with	  or	  
without	  different	  concentrations	  of	  Ipilimumab,	  Nivolumab	  and	  Ipilimumab	  +	  Nivolumab.	  The	  presented	  data	  is	  
collected	  from	  three	  days	  incubation	  (day	  one	  left	  –	  day	  three	  right).	  
As	  Figure	  38	  shows	  the	  cells	  that	  are	  not	  treated	  also	  has	  a	  basic	  production	  of	  IFN-­‐	  γ,	  but	  this	  
production	  increases	  upon	  the	  addition	  of	  Ipilimumab,	  Nivolumab	  or	  a	  combination	  of	  
Ipilimumab	  and	  Nivolumab.	  This	  increase	  seems	  to	  be	  at	  the	  highest	  at	  day	  two	  for	  Ipilimumab	  
and	  Nivolumab	  and	  at	  day	  three	  for	  the	  combination	  treatment.	  In	  this	  experiment	  a	  technical	  
problem	  occurred	  and	  because	  of	  that	  the	  results	  lacks	  from	  the	  samples	  with;	  10µg/ml	  
Ipilimumab,	  20	  µg/ml	  Nivolumab	  and	  10	  µg/ml	  Nivolumab	  and	  5	  µg/ml	  of	  the	  combination	  
treatment	  (Ipilimumab	  and	  Nivolumab)	  all	  at	  day	  three	  of	  incubation.	  
Binding	  assay	  
In	  this	  assay	  PBMCs	  from	  both	  human	  and	  pig	  were	  stimulated	  with	  0.1µg/ml	  SEB	  and	  
incubated	  for	  different	  time	  intervals	  (three	  hours,	  one	  day,	  two	  days,	  three	  days	  and	  four	  days)	  
to	  investigate	  the	  binding	  and	  difference	  in	  CTLA-­‐4	  and	  PD-­‐1protein	  amount	  due	  to	  stimulation	  
over	  time.	  Humane	  PBMCs	  were	  used	  as	  positive	  control	  and	  un-­‐stimulated	  porcine	  and	  human	  
PBMCs	  with	  no	  Ipilimumab/Nivolumab	  were	  used	  as	  the	  negative	  control.	  The	  samples	  with	  no	  
checkpoint	  inhibitor	  antibody	  (Ipilimumab	  or	  Nivolumab)	  contain	  the	  secondary	  biotin	  
conjugated	  IgG	  (H+L)	  monoclonal	  antibody.	  
Dot-­‐blot	  assay	  
First	  a	  dot-­‐blot	  was	  done	  to	  investigate	  the	  binding	  of	  Ipilimumab	  and	  Nivolumab	  to	  the	  
secondary	  antibody	  (biotinylated	  goat	  Anti-­‐human	  IgG(H+L))	  called	  in	  this	  study	  @IgG.	  As	  a	  
result	  of	  this,	  color	  was	  obtained	  in	  all	  spots	  except	  the	  negative	  control	  which	  indicates	  that	  the	  
primary	  antibodies	  (Ipilimumab	  and	  Nivolumab)	  binds	  to	  the	  secondary	  @IgG	  and	  the	  @IgG	  
binds	  alkaline	  phosphatase	  conjugated	  streptavidin.	  
==PAGE:61==
	  
49  
Binding	  assay	  by	  Flow	  Cytometry	  	  
After	  sample	  processing	  and	  fixation	  all	  samples	  ran	  in	  FACSCanto	  II,	  and	  all	  samples	  
were	  analyzed	  using	  FACS	  Diva	  software	  6.1	  (BD).	  	  Cells	  with	  no	  Ipilimumab	  nor	  Nivolumab	  or	  
SEB	  were	  used	  to	  gate	  for	  the	  events	  with	  CD3+	  Ab+,	  CD4+Ab+	  and	  CD8+Ab+	  (Ab	  is	  Ipilimumab	  
or	  Nivolumab)	  in	  different	  plots.	  Fluorescence	  intensities	  of	  approximately	  2000	  to	  150,000	  
cells	  	  (live,	  lymphocytes	  and	  single	  events)	  per	  sample	  were	  measured.	  	  All	  samples	  were	  made	  
in	  duplicates	  and	  average	  and	  standard	  deviation	  was	  measured	  for	  these.	  Some	  of	  the	  samples	  
have	  no	  duplicate	  due	  to	  pipetting	  error	  these	  samples	  has	  no	  SDs,	  they	  are	  shown	  as	  points	  
with	  no	  SD	  in	  the	  charts	  that	  presents	  the	  results	  in	  this	  assay.	  
Results	  for	  the	  binding	  of	  Ipilimumab	  and	  Nivolumab	  to	  human	  lymphocytes	  
Data	  was	  analyzed	  by	  setting	  a	  gate	  around	  life	  cells,	  gate	  around	  the	  lymphocytes	  (on	  the	  basis	  
of	  forward	  scatter	  and	  sideward	  scatter)	  after	  exclusion	  of	  the	  dead	  cell	  population	  and	  a	  gate	  
around	  single	  cells	  (on	  the	  basis	  of	  FSC-­‐A	  and	  FSC-­‐H)	  see	  Figure	  39.	  CD3+CD4+,	  CD3+CD8+,	  
CD3+CD4+Ipilimumab/Nivolumab+,	  CD3+CD8+	  Ipilimumab/Nivolumab+	  and	  CD3+	  
Ipilimumab/Nivolumab+	  cells	  were	  distinguished	  and	  the	  median	  fluorescence	  intensities	  (MFI)	  
and	  %	  of	  the	  parent	  population	  was	  calculated.	  FACS	  Diva	  software	  6.1	  (BD)	  and	  EXCEL	  were	  
used	  to	  analyze	  the	  data.	  All	  gates	  were	  placed	  according	  to	  the	  samples	  with	  no	  checkpoint	  
inhibitor	  antibody	  neither	  SEB	  (negative	  controls).	  Figure	  40	  presents	  an	  example	  for	  the	  gating	  
of	  samples	  from	  48-­‐hour	  incubation	  without	  Ipilimumab,	  Nivolumab	  nor	  SEB.	  To	  show	  the	  
difference	  in	  the	  flow	  cytometry	  analysis	  in	  plots	  Figure	  41	  presents	  the	  data	  from	  the	  same	  
incubation	  time	  but	  with	  stimulated	  samples.	  
	  
Figure	  39:	  plots	  that	  show	  an	  example	  of	  the	  gating	  of	  live,	  single	  cells	  and	  lymphocytes.	  The	  diagram	  to	  the	  right	  
shows	  the	  gating	  of	  life	  cells	  excluding	  dead	  cells,	  the	  middle	  plot	  shows	  single	  cells	  found	  from	  forward	  scatter	  (areal	  
and	  height)	  and	  the	  plot	  to	  the	  left	  shows	  the	  lymphocytes	  based	  on	  both	  forward	  and	  side	  scatter.	  
The	  plots	  that	  are	  incubated	  with	  SEB	  as	  well	  as	  plots	  that	  are	  not	  stimulated	  shows	  that	  there	  
are	  CD3-­‐	  events	  that	  has	  the	  fluorochrome	  PE	  and	  binds	  to	  the	  secondary	  biotinylated	  IgG(H+L).	  
The	  plots	  in	  Figure	  41	  with	  the	  stimulated	  cells	  that	  are	  stained	  with	  Ipilimumab	  show	  higher	  
events	  then	  in	  un-­‐stimulated	  cells.	  This	  pattern	  was	  also	  observed	  for	  Nivolumab	  and	  indicates	  
the	  binding	  of	  both	  Ipilimumab	  and	  Nivolumab	  to	  the	  lymphocytes.	  To	  present	  the	  data	  of	  this	  
assay	  different	  charts	  were	  made.	  
A	  total	  of	  approximately	  30,000-­‐120,000	  events	  were	  analyzed	  in	  exception	  for	  samples	  with	  48	  
hours	  incubation,	  where	  lowest	  events	  were	  measured	  (5500-­‐48,000).	  The	  percentage	  of	  events	  
that	  represent	  CD3	  stained	  cells	  were	  between	  70-­‐80	  %,	  and	  about	  30%-­‐35%	  and	  60%-­‐65%	  for	  
CD8	  and	  CD4	  respectively.	  
==PAGE:62==

Figure	  40:	  the	  plots	  show	  the	  populations	  of	  CD3,	  CD4	  and	  CD8	  cells.	  First	  CD3	  was	  distinguished	  from	  lymphocytes	  
by	  the	  fluorochrome	  BV	  421	  and	  this	  population	  was	  gated,	  then	  CD-­‐4	  and	  CD8	  were	  gated	  out	  of	  the	  CD-­‐3	  population	  
by	  their	  fluorochromes.	  The	  Ab	  stands	  for	  checkpoint	  inhibitor	  antibody	  (Ipilimumab	  or	  Nivolumab).	  The	  populations	  
that	  have	  the	  fluorochrome	  PE	  represent	  the	  Ab	  that	  was	  gated	  for	  in	  each	  of	  the	  populations	  CD3+,	  CD3+	  CD8+,	  CD3+	  
CD4+	  (Ab	  CD3,	  Ab	  CD8,	  Ab	  CD4	  in	  the	  plots).	  The	  samples	  used	  in	  this	  example	  were	  incubated	  for	  48	  hours	  with	  no	  
Ipilimumab,	  no	  Nivolumab	  and	  no	  SEB.

Figure	  41:	  these	  plots	  shows	  the	  populations	  (events)	  for	  each	  of	  CD3+,	  CD3+	  CD8+,	  CD3+	  CD4+	  ,Ab	  CD3,	  Ab	  CD8,	  Ab	  
CD4	  for	  human	  PBMCs	  stimulated	  with	  0.1µg/ml	  SEB	  for	  48	  hours	  and	  stained	  with	  the	  Ab	  Ipilimumab.	  
The	  FACS	  Diva	  software	  calculated	  the	  parent	  %	  of	  all	  events.	  The	  mean	  parent	  %	  and	  mean	  MFI	  
was	  calculated	  for	  all	  duplicates	  and	  the	  standard	  deviation	  was	  found.	  	  
To	  analyze	  the	  binding	  of	  Ipilimumab	  and	  Nivolumab	  to	  CD3+	  cells,	  the	  parent	  %	  of	  the	  CD3+	  
Ab+	  	  and	  CD3+	  Ab-­‐	  	  were	  plotted	  against	  time	  for	  both	  stimulated	  and	  un-­‐stimulated	  samples.	  
Figure	  42	  presents	  the	  obtained	  results	  with	  the	  standard	  deviation	  bars.	  
The	  results	  indicates	  a	  binding	  for	  Nivolumab	  already	  after	  three	  hours	  in	  stimulated	  cells,	  and	  
the	  parent	  %	  increases	  over	  time	  to	  reach	  the	  maximum	  after	  four	  days.	  The	  same	  pattern	  is	  
shown	  for	  un-­‐stimulated	  cells	  but	  with	  lower	  parent	  %.	  	  
As	  for	  Ipilimumab,	  a	  low	  parent	  %	  was	  obtained	  after	  three	  hours	  incubation	  with	  SEB	  but	  
already	  after	  24	  hours	  an	  increase	  in	  the	  parent	  %	  Ipilimumab	  bound	  to	  CD3	  is	  found	  and	  the	  
increase	  continued	  reaching	  the	  top	  at	  day	  two	  only	  to	  begin	  to	  decrease	  again	  afterwards.	  The	  
parent	  %	  never	  reaches	  the	  start	  percentage	  after	  four	  days.	  In	  samples	  with	  no	  SEB	  the	  same	  
pattern	  is	  also	  observed	  but	  with	  lower	  parent	  %.	  The	  background	  is	  shown	  in	  the	  plot	  by	  the	  
lines	  that	  present	  samples	  that	  were	  not	  stained	  with	  Ipilimumab	  or	  Nivolumab.

Figure	  43:	  Chart	  that	  describes	  the	  parent	  event	  %	  of	  CD8-­‐checkpoint	  inhibitor	  antibodies	  out	  of	  CD8	  stained	  cells	  
with	  or	  without	  SEB.	  The	  columns	  without	  SD	  present	  the	  samples	  that	  have	  no	  duplicates.	  
Another	  analysis	  that	  was	  carried	  out	  with	  the	  obtained	  results	  from	  the	  FACs	  analysis	  is	  the	  
mean	  fluorescent	  Intensity	  of	  all	  events	  that	  were	  stained	  with	  CD3	  antibodies	  and	  Ipilimumab,	  
Nivolumab	  or	  no	  checkpoint	  inhibitor	  antibody,	  see	  Figure	  45.	  The	  results	  of	  this	  analysis	  
indicates	  that	  for	  Nivolumab	  the	  MFI	  increases	  in	  SEB	  stimulated	  cells	  over	  time	  only	  to	  reach

Ipilimumab	  MFI	  in	  stimulated	  and	  un-­‐stimulated	  cells	  has	  the	  same	  pattern	  with	  higher	  values	  in	  
the	  stimulated	  cells	  where	  an	  increase	  in	  MFI	  is	  observed	  after	  one	  day	  incubation	  and	  reaches	  
the	  maximum	  after	  48	  hours.	  These	  results	  resample	  the	  results	  from	  the	  parent	  %	  analysis	  for	  
both	  Ipilimumab	  and	  Nivolumab.	  As	  for	  the	  negative	  controls	  the	  MFI	  is	  high	  at	  the	  beginning	  
==PAGE:65==
	  
53  
and	  decreases	  rapidly.	  There	  was	  no	  Ipilimumab	  neither	  Nivolumab	  in	  these	  samples	  but	  there	  
was	  the	  secondary	  anti-­‐human	  biotinylated	  IgG	  (H+L),	  either	  it	  was	  an	  error	  in	  pipetting	  or	  
unspecific	  binding,	  but	  still	  low	  parent	  %	  in	  these	  samples	  (low	  amount	  of	  events)	  was	  obtained.

Results	  for	  the	  binding	  of	  Ipilimumab	  and	  Nivolumab	  to	  porcine	  lymphocytes	  
The	  data	  obtained	  from	  pig	  samples	  were	  analyzed	  in	  the	  same	  way	  as	  for	  human	  samples.	  See	  
Figure	  46	  for	  an	  example	  of	  the	  gating	  for	  live	  lymphocytes	  single	  cells	  and	  Figure	  47	  for	  an

the	  difference	  in	  the	  flow	  Cytometry	  analysis	  in	  plots	  Figure	  48	  presents	  the	  data	  from	  the	  same

analyze	  the	  checkpoint	  inhibitor	  antibodies	  in	  porcine	  samples	  is	  APC.	  
	  
==PAGE:66==
	  
54  
	  
Figure	  46:	  plots	  that	  shows	  the	  gating	  of	  live,	  single	  cells	  and	  lymphocytes.	  The	  diagram	  to	  the	  right	  shows	  the	  gating	  
of	  life	  cells	  excluding	  dead	  cells,	  the	  middle	  plot	  shows	  single	  cells	  found	  from	  forward	  scatter	  (areal	  and	  hight)	  and	  
the	  plot	  to	  the	  left	  shows	  the	  lymphocytes	  based	  on	  both	  forward	  and	  side	  scatter.	  
The	  PBMCs	  that	  are	  incubated	  with	  SEB	  as	  well	  as	  PBMCs	  that	  are	  not	  stimulated	  shows	  that	  
there	  are	  CD3	  -­‐	  events	  that	  have	  the	  fluorochrome	  APC	  and	  bind	  to	  the	  secondary	  biotinylated	  
IgG(H+L).	  The	  plots	  in	  Figure	  48	  with	  the	  stimulated	  and	  stained	  with	  Ipilimumab	  cells	  shows	  
not	  much	  more	  events	  with	  Ipilimumab	  and	  Nivolumab	  than	  in	  un-­‐stimulated	  samples.	  This	  
could	  indicate	  an	  unspecific	  binding	  of	  the	  anti-­‐human	  biotin	  conjugated	  secondary	  antibody	  IgG	  
(H+L)	  as	  there	  is	  relatively	  to	  human	  samples	  high	  APC	  fluorescents	  in	  samples	  with	  no	  
checkpoint	  inhibition	  antibodies.	  In	  this	  analysis	  half	  the	  amount	  of	  the	  staining	  antibody	  for	  
CD4	  was	  used	  which	  may	  cause	  insufficient	  staining,	  another	  important	  matter	  in	  this	  assay	  is	  
that	  for	  24	  hour	  incubation	  samples,	  the	  amount	  of	  CD3	  staining	  secondary	  antibody	  was	  too	  
low	  which	  led	  to	  no	  separation	  in	  the	  lymphocyte	  population	  so	  for	  the	  samples	  from	  24	  hours	  
all	  lymphocytes	  were	  investigated	  for	  the	  binding	  of	  Ipilimumab	  and	  Nivolumab.	  	  
The	  data	  was	  calculated	  and	  is	  presented	  in	  the	  same	  way	  as	  for	  human	  samples.	  Different	  
charts	  were	  made	  and	  approximately	  20,000-­‐40,000	  (live	  single	  lymphocytes)	  events	  were	  
analyzed	  in	  exception	  for	  samples	  from	  48	  hours	  incubation,	  where	  lowest	  events	  were	  
measured	  (2700-­‐40,000).	  The	  percentage	  of	  CD3	  stained	  cells	  were	  between	  70-­‐80	  %,	  events	  
that	  were	  stained	  for	  CD8	  and	  CD4	  made	  about	  11%-­‐20%	  and	  4%-­‐9%	  respectively.	  In	  porcine	  
lymphocytes	  CD3+	  γδ	  cells	  exist,	  more	  about	  this	  fact	  will	  be	  discussed	  in	  the	  discussion	  section.	  
The	  FACs	  Diva	  software	  calculated	  the	  parent%	  of	  all	  events,	  the	  mean	  and	  SD	  for	  the	  duplicates	  
were	  calculated	  and	  used	  in	  the	  data	  analysis.	  To	  analyze	  the	  binding	  of	  Ipilimumab	  and	  
Nivolumab	  to	  CD3+	  cells,	  the	  parent	  %	  of	  the	  CD3+	  Ab+	  and	  CD3+	  Ab-­‐	  were	  plotted	  against	  time	  
for	  both	  stimulated	  and	  un-­‐stimulated	  samples.

Summery	  of	  the	  result	  
To	  sum	  up	  the	  results,	  a	  table	  (Table	  13)	  has	  been	  made	  with	  the	  results	  from	  the	  data	  
analysis	  of	  the	  different	  assays,	  taken	  into	  consideration	  that	  all	  assays	  were	  performed	  
in	  one	  subject	  and	  only	  conducted	  one	  time.	  Additionally,	  any	  unspecific	  binding	  of	  the	  
secondary	  antibody	  to	  other	  cell	  types	  and	  other	  receptors	  on	  CD3	  +	  cells	  together	  with	  
the	  practical	  errors	  made	  through	  the	  analysis	  and	  the	  standard	  deviations	  were	  taken	  
into	  account.
